## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position, velocity, and time. The equation of motion for such systems typically involves restoring forces (functions of x), damping terms (functions of v), and possibly driving forces (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Cubic nonlinear restoring force (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (Duffing oscillator without damping)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing oscillator with linear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillator with nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Combined nonlinear terms: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (coupled nonlinear terms)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Driven oscillator with nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * (1 - x**2) * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven Van der Pol-Duffing)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (multiplicative coupling between position and velocity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) â†’ symmetric potential wells preserving oscillatory symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - x**2)*v â†’ amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of limit cycle oscillators (Van der Pol type)
- Cubic position term x**3 with opposite sign to linear term â†’ double-well potential or hardening/softening spring (Duffing type)
- Periodic driving terms cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) â†’ externally forced oscillation leading to resonance or chaos
- Odd velocity damping (v, v**3) â†’ energy dissipation preserving time-reversal symmetry structure
- Product terms x*v or x**2*v â†’ nonlinear energy transfer between kinetic and potential modes
- Absence of explicit time dependence â†’ autonomous system with conserved or slowly varying energy
- Sign of the linear x coefficient determines stability: negative coefficient â†’ stable equilibrium, positive â†’ unstable

Candidate 15 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 16: `c0*x + c1*sin(t) + c2*sin(c3*v) + c4*x*(c5 + v)**3`
